\topts[\"THIS_INTERFACE_MAC_2\"] = uint64(sliceToBe16(mac[4:6]))\n194: \n195: \tifIndex := uint32(iface.Attrs().Index)\n196: \n197: \tif !option.Config.EnableHostLegacyRouting {\n198: \t\topts[\"SECCTX_FROM_IPCACHE\"] = uint64(secctxFromIpcacheEnabled)\n199: \t} else {\n200: \t\topts[\"SECCTX_FROM_IPCACHE\"] = uint64(secctxFromIpcacheDisabled)\n201: \t}\n202: \n203: \t// Overwrite the host endpoint ifindex assigned in ELFVariableSubstitutions\n204: \t// with the external device's.\n205: \topts[\"interface_ifindex\"] = uint64(ifIndex)\n206: \n207: \tif option.Config.EnableBPFMasquerade && ifName != defaults.SecondHostDevice {\n208: \t\tipv4, ipv6 := bpfMasqAddrs(ifName, cfg)\n209: \n210: \t\tif option.Config.EnableIPv4Masquerade && ipv4.IsValid() {\n211: \t\t\topts[\"IPV4_MASQUERADE\"] = uint64(byteorder.NetIPv4ToHost32(ipv4.AsSlice()))\n212: \t\t}\n213: \t\tif option.Config.EnableIPv6Masquerade && ipv6.IsValid() {\n214: \t\t\tipv6Bytes := ipv6.AsSlice()\n215: \t\t\topts[\"IPV6_MASQUERADE_1\"] = sliceToBe64(ipv6Bytes[0:8])\n216: \t\t\topts[\"IPV6_MASQUERADE_2\"] = sliceToBe64(ipv6Bytes[8:16])\n217: \t\t}\n218: \t}\n219: \n220: \tcallsMapHostDevice := bpf.LocalMapName(callsmap.HostMapName, templateLxcID)\n221: \tstrings[callsMapHostDevice] = bpf.LocalMapName(callsmap.NetdevMapName, uint16(ifIndex))\n222: \n223: \treturn opts, strings, nil\n224: }\n225: \n226: func isObsoleteDev(dev string, devices []string) bool {\n227: \t// exclude devices we never attach to/from_netdev to.\n228: \tfor _, prefix := range defaults.ExcludedDevicePrefixes {\n229: \t\tif strings.HasPrefix(dev, prefix) {\n230: \t\t\treturn false\n231: \t\t}\n232: \t}\n233: \n234: \t// exclude devices that will still be managed going forward.\n235: \tfor _, d := range devices {\n236: \t\tif dev == d {\n237: \t\t\treturn false\n238: \t\t}\n239: \t}\n240: \n241: \treturn true\n242: }\n243: \n244: // removeObsoleteNetdevPrograms removes cil_to_netdev and cil_from_netdev from devices\n245: // that cilium potentially doesn't manage anymore after a restart, e.g. if the set of\n246: // devices changes between restarts.\n247: //\n248: // This code assumes that the agent was upgraded from a prior version while maintaining\n249: // the same list of managed physical devices. This ensures that all tc bpf filters get\n250: // replaced using the naming convention of the 'current' agent build. For example,\n251: // before 1.13, most filters were named e.g. bpf_host.o:[to-host], to be changed to\n252: // cilium-<device> in 1.13, then to cil_to_host-<device> in 1.14. As a result, this\n253: // function only cleans up filters following the current naming scheme.\n254: func removeObsoleteNetdevPrograms(devices []string) error {\n255: \tlinks, err := safenetlink.LinkList()\n256: \tif err != nil {\n257: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"retrieving all netlink devices: %w\", err)\n258: \t}\n259: \n260: \t// collect all devices that have netdev programs attached on either ingress or egress.\n261: \tingressDevs := []netlink.Link{}\n262: \tegressDevs := []netlink.Link{}\n263: \tfor _, l := range links {\n264: \t\tif !isObsoleteDev(l.Attrs().Name, devices) {\n265: \t\t\tcontinue\n266: \t\t}\n267: \n268: \t\t// Remove the per-device bpffs directory containing pinned links and\n269: \t\t// per-endpoint maps.\n270: \t\tbpffsPath := bpffsDeviceDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), l)\n271: \t\tif err := bpf.Remove(bpffsPath); err != nil {\n272: \t\t\tlog.WithError(err).WithField(logfields.Device, l.Attrs().Name)\n273: \t\t}\n274: \n275: \t\tingressFilters, err := safenetlink.FilterList(l, directionToParent(dirIngress))\n276: \t\tif err != nil {\n277: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"listing ingress filters: %w\", err)\n278: \t\t}\n279: \t\tfor _, filter := range ingressFilters {\n280: \t\t\tif bpfFilter, ok := filter.(*netlink.BpfFilter); ok {\n281: \t\t\t\tif strings.HasPrefix(bpfFilter.Name, symbolFromHostNetdevEp) {\n282: \t\t\t\t\tingressDevs = append(ingressDevs, l)\n283: \t\t\t\t}\n284: \t\t\t}\n285: \t\t}\n286: \n287: \t\tegressFilters, err := safenetlink.FilterList(l, directionToParent(dirEgress))\n288: \t\tif err != nil {\n289: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"listing egress filters: %w\", err)\n290: \t\t}\n291: \t\tfor _, filter := range egressFilters {\n292: \t\t\tif bpfFilter, ok := filter.(*netlink.BpfFilter); ok {\n293: \t\t\t\tif strings.HasPrefix(bpfFilter.Name, symbolToHostNetdevEp) {\n294: \t\t\t\t\tegressDevs = append(egressDevs, l)\n295: \t\t\t\t}\n296: \t\t\t}\n297: \t\t}\n298: \t}\n299: \n300: \tfor _, dev := range ingressDevs {\n301: \t\terr = removeTCFilters(dev, directionToParent(dirIngress))\n302: \t\tif err != nil {\n303: \t\t\tlog.WithError(err).Errorf(\"couldn't remove ingress tc filters from %s\", dev.Attrs().Name)\n304: \t\t}\n305: \t}\n306: \n307: \tfor _, dev := range egressDevs {\n308: \t\terr = removeTCFilters(dev, directionToParent(dirEgress))\n309: \t\tif err != nil {\n310: \t\t\tlog.WithError(err).Errorf(\"couldn't remove egress tc filters from %s\", dev.Attrs().Name)\n311: \t\t}\n312: \t}\n313: \n314: \treturn nil\n315: }\n316: \n317: // reloadHostEndpoint (re)attaches programs from bpf_host.c to cilium_host,\n318: // cilium_net and external (native) devices.\n319: func reloadHostEndpoint(cfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration, ep datapath.Endpoint, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec) error {\n320: \t// Replace programs on cilium_host.\n321: \tif err := attachCiliumHost(ep, spec); err != nil {\n322: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"attaching cilium_host: %w\", err)\n323: \t}\n324: \n325: \tif err := attachCiliumNet(cfg, ep, spec); err != nil {\n326: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"attaching cilium_host: %w\", err)\n327: \t}\n328: \n329: \tif err := attachNetworkDevices(cfg, ep, spec); err != nil {\n330: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"attaching cilium_host: %w\", err)\n331: \t}\n332: \n333: \treturn nil\n334: }\n335: \n336: // attachCiliumHost inserts the host endpoint's policy program into the global\n337: // cilium_call_policy map and attaches programs from bpf_host.c to cilium_host.\n338: func attachCiliumHost(ep datapath.Endpoint, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec) error {\n339: \thost, err := safenetlink.LinkByName(ep.InterfaceName())\n340: \tif err != nil {\n341: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"retrieving device %s: %w\", ep.InterfaceName(), err)\n342: \t}\n343: \n344: \tvar hostObj hostObjects\n345: \tcommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(&hostObj, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n346: \t\tCollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n347: \t\t\tMaps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.TCGlobalsPath()},\n348: \t\t},\n349: \t\tMapRenames: ELFMapSubstitutions(ep),\n350: \t\tConstants:  ELFVariableSubstitutions(ep),\n351: \t})\n352: \tif err != nil {\n353: \t\treturn err\n354: \t}\n355: \tdefer hostObj.Close()\n356: \n357: \t// Insert host endpoint policy program.\n358: \tif err := hostObj.PolicyMap.Update(uint32(ep.GetID()), hostObj.PolicyProg, ebpf.UpdateAny); Attaches cil_from_netdev to ingress and\n420: // optionally cil_to_netdev to egress if enabled features require it.\n421: func attachNetworkDevices(cfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration, ep datapath.Endpoint, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec) error {\n422: \tdevices := cfg.DeviceNames()\n423: \n424: \t// Selectively attach bpf_host to cilium_wg0.\n425: \tif option.Config.NeedBPFHostOnWireGuardDevice() {\n426: \t\tdevices = append(devices, wgTypes.IfaceName)\n427: \t}\n428: \n429: \t// Replace programs on physical devices, ignoring devices that don't exist.\n430: \tfor _, device := range devices {\n431: \t\tiface, err := safenetlink.LinkByName(device)\n432: \t\tif err != nil {\n433: \t\t\tlog.WithError(err).WithField(\"device\", device).Warn(\"Link does not exist\")\n434: \t\t\tcontinue\n435: \t\t}\n436: \n437: \t\tlinkDir := bpffsDeviceLinksDir(bpf.CiliumPath(), iface)\n438: \n439: \t\tconsts, renames, err := hostRewrites(cfg, ep, device)\n440: \t\tif err != nil {\n441: \t\t\treturn err\n442: \t\t}\n443: \n444: \t\tvar netdevObj hostNetdevObjects\n445: \t\tcommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(&netdevObj, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n446: \t\t\tCollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n447: \t\t\t\tMaps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.TCGlobalsPath()},\n448: \t\t\t},\n449: \t\t\tMapRenames: renames,\n450: \t\t\tConstants:  consts,\n451: \t\t})\n452: \t\tif err != nil {\n453: \t\t\treturn err\n454: \t\t}\n455: \t\tdefer netdevObj.Close()\n456: \n457: \t\t// Attach cil_from_netdev to ingress.\n458: \t\tif err := attachSKBProgram(iface, netdevObj.FromNetdev, symbolFromHostNetdevEp,\n459: \t\t\tlinkDir, netlink.HANDLE_MIN_INGRESS, option.Config.EnableTCX); err != nil {\n489: \t\t\t\tlog.WithField(\"device\", device).Error(err)\n490: \t\t\t}\n491: \t\t}\n492: \n493: \t\tif err := commit(); err != nil {\n494: \t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"committing bpf pins: %w\", err)\n495: \t\t}\n496: \t}\n497: \n498: \t// Call immediately after attaching programs to make it obvious that a\n499: \t// program was wrongfully detached due to a bug or misconfiguration.\n500: \tif err := removeObsoleteNetdevPrograms(devices); err != nil {\n501: \t\tlog.WithError(err).Error(\"Failed to remove obsolete netdev programs\")\n502: \t}\n503: \n504: \treturn nil\n505: }\n506: \n507: // reloadEndpoint loads programs in spec into the device used by ep.\n508: //\n509: // spec is modified by the method and it is the callers responsibility to copy\n510: // it if necessary.\n511: func reloadEndpoint(ep datapath.Endpoint, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec) error {\n512: \tdevice := ep.InterfaceName()\n513: \n514: \tvar obj lxcObjects\n515: \tcommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(&obj, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n516: \t\tCollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n517: \t\t\tMaps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.TCGlobalsPath()},\n518: \t\t},\n519: \t\tMapRenames: ELFMapSubstitutions(ep),\n520: \t\tConstants:  ELFVariableSubstitutions(ep),\n521: \t})\n522: \tif err != nil {\n523: \t\treturn err\n524: \t}\n525: \tdefer obj.Close()\n526: \n527: \t// Insert policy programs before attaching entrypoints to tc hooks.\n528: \t// Inserting a policy program is considered an attachment, since it makes\n529: \t// the code reachable by bpf_host when it evaluates policy for the endpoint.\n530: \t// All internal tail call plumbing needs to be done before this point.\n531: \t// If the agent dies uncleanly after the first program has been inserted,\n532: \t// the endpoint's connectivity will be partially broken or exhibit undefined\n533: \t// behaviour like missed tail calls or drops.\n534: \tif err := obj.PolicyMap.Update(uint32(ep.GetID()), obj.PolicyProg, ebpf.UpdateAny); err != nil {\n559: \t\t\tlog.WithField(\"device\", device).Error(err)\n560: \t\t}\n561: \t}\n562: \n563: \tif err := commit(); err != nil {\n564: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"committing bpf pins: %w\", err)\n565: \t}\n566: \n567: \tif ep.RequireEndpointRoute() {\n568: \t\tscopedLog := ep.Logger(subsystem).WithFields(logrus.Fields{\n569: \t\t\tlogfields.Interface: device,\n570: \t\t})\n571: \t\tif ip := ep.IPv4Address(); see\n99: \t// iptables.addCiliumENIRules().\n100: \t// The default AWS daemonset installs the following rules that are used\n101: \t// for NodePort traffic between nodes:\n102: \t//\n103: \t// # sysctl -w net.ipv4.conf.eth0.rp_filter=2\n104: \t// # iptables -t mangle -A PREROUTING -i eth0 -m comment --comment \"AWS, primary ENI\" -m addrtype --dst-type LOCAL --limit-iface-in -j CONNMARK --set-xmark 0x80/0x80\n105: \t// # iptables -t mangle -A PREROUTING -i eni+ -m comment --comment \"AWS, primary ENI\" -j CONNMARK --restore-mark --nfmask 0x80 --ctmask 0x80\n106: \t// # ip rule add fwmark 0x80/0x80 lookup main\n107: \t//\n108: \t// It marks packets coming from another node through eth0, and restores\n109: \t// the mark on the return path to force a lookup into the main routing\n110: \t// table. \t\t}()\n666: \t} else {\n667: \t\tclose(datapathRegenCtxt.ctCleaned)\n668: \t}\n669: \n670: \t// Set the computed policy as the \"incoming\" policy. This can fail if\n671: \t// the endpoint's security identity changed during or after policy calculation.\n672: \t// Note that the incoming policy can be the same as the previous policy in cases\n673: \t// where an unnecessary policy computation was skipped. In that case\n674: \t// e.desiredPolicy == e.realizedPolicy also after this call.\n675: \tif err := e.setDesiredPolicy(datapathRegenCtxt); err != nil {\n676: \t\treturn err\n677: \t}\n678: \t// Mark the new desired policy as ready when done before the lock is released\n679: \tif e.desiredPolicy != e.realizedPolicy {\n680: \t\tdefer e.desiredPolicy.Ready()\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \t// Apply pending policy map changes so that desired map is up-to-date before\n684: \t// syncing the maps below.\n685: \tif e.SecurityIdentity != nil {\n686: \t\t_ = e.updateAndOverrideEndpointOptions(nil)\n687: \n688: \t\t// Apply incremental changes to desiredPolicy and Configure the new network policy\n689: \t\t// with the proxies.\n690: \t\t//\n691: \t\t// If we have a new policy, it is likely that incremental updates were applied to\n692: \t\t// the old policy while we were waiting for the endpoint lock. If we were to sync\n693: \t\t// policy maps without applying incremental updates first we could be flapping\n694: \t\t// network policy backwards just to be updating it again after applying incremental\n695: \t\t// updates later.\n696: \t\t//\n697: \t\t// This must be done after adding new redirects, as waiting for policy update\n698: \t\t// ACKs is disabled when there are no listeners, which is the case before the first\n699: \t\t// redirect is added.\n700: \t\t//\n701: \t\t// Do this before updating the bpf policy maps (later), so that the proxy listeners\n702: \t\t// have a chance to be ready when new traffic is redirected to them.  Note that it\n703: \t\t// is possible for further incremental changes to be applied before and after the\n704: \t\t// bpf policy maps have been synchronized for the new policy.\n705: \t\terr = e.applyPolicyMapChangesLocked(regenContext, e.desiredPolicy != e.realizedPolicy)\n706: \t\tif err != nil && !errors.Is(err, ErrPolicyEntryMaxExceeded) {\n707: \t\t\treturn err\n708: \t\t}\n709: \n710: \t\t// Signal computation of the initial Envoy policy if not done yet\n711: \t\te.initialPolicyComputedLocked()\n712: \t}\n713: \n714: \tcurrentDir := datapathRegenCtxt.currentDir\n715: \tnextDir := datapathRegenCtxt.nextDir\n716: \n717: \t// We cannot obtain the rules while e.mutex is held, because obtaining\n718: \t// fresh DNSRules requires the IPCache lock (which must not be taken while\n719: \t// holding e.mutex to avoid deadlocks). performed\n724: \tif e.isProperty(PropertySkipBPFPolicy) {\n725: \t\t// Ingress endpoint needs epInfoCache for endpointmap population\n726: \t\tif e.isProperty(PropertyAtHostNS) {\n727: {\n732: \t\t\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"Unable to write header file: %w\", err)\n733: \t\t\t}\n734: \t\t}\n735: \t\treturn nil\n736: \t}\n737: \n738: \tif e.policyMap == nil {\n739: \t\te.policyMap, err = \tif e.realizedPolicy != e.desiredPolicy && e.realizedPolicy.Empty() {\n747: \t\tdatapathRegenCtxt.policyMapDump, err = e.dumpPolicyMapToMapStateMap()\n748: \t\tif err != nil {\n749: \t\t\treturn downgrades from versions using a different policy map\n754: \t\tif len(datapathRegenCtxt.policyMapDump) == 0 {\n755: \t\t\terr = e.policyMapSync(nil, stats)\n756: \t\t\tif err != nil {\n757: in map to allow all ingress/egress traffic, something like this:\n764: \t\t\t//  PROXY PORT   AUTH TYPE   BYTES   PACKETS   PREFIX\n766: \t\t\t// Allow    Ingress     ANY                           ANY          NONE         disabled    2426    29        0\n767: \t\t\t// Allow    Ingress     reserved:host                 ANY          NONE         disabled    0       0         0\n768: \t\t\t// Allow    Egress      ANY                           ANY          NONE         disabled    30639   165       0\n769: \t\t\t// ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------\n770: \t\t\t// If the code has reached here, it means:\n771: \t\t\t// 1. The endpoint has a policy map that is not empty (default policy exists)\n772: \t\t\t// 2. No policies has been realized (realized policy is empty)\n773: \t\t\t// 3. New policies need to be applied for this endpoint (hence desiredPolicy != realizedPolicy)\n774: \t\t\t// GH-37724: https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/37724\n775: \t\t\te.getLogger().Debug(\n776: \t\t\t\t\"Policy map is not empty, but no policy has been realized yet, setting policyMapSyncDone to false\",\n777: \t\t\t)\n778: \t\t\t// Ensure that e.realizedPolicy actually represents the\n779: \t\t\t// current policy map state in case rollback is\n780: \t\t\t// necessary, so we don't try to \"roll back\" to an empty\n781: \t\t\t// map and delete all the entries, even momentarily.\n782: \t\t\t// This may be the case if the agent just restarted,\n783: \t\t\t// for example. It returns one special error\n1115: // that must be considered, \"ErrPolicyEntryMaxExceeded\".\n1116: func (e *Endpoint) applyPolicyMapChangesLocked(regenContext *regenerationContext, hasNewPolicy bool) error {\n1117: \te.PolicyDebug(nil, \"applyPolicyMapChanges\")\n1118: \n1119: \t// Always update Envoy if policy has changed\n1120: \tupdateEnvoy := hasNewPolicy\n1121: \n1122: \t// Note that after successful endpoint regeneration the desired and realized policies are\n1123: \t// the same pointer. During the bpf regeneration possible incremental updates are collected\n1124: \t// on the newly computed desired policy, which is not fully realized yet. This is why we get\n1125: \t// the map changes from the desired policy here.\n1126: \n1127: \t// ConsumeMapChanges() applies the incremental updates to the desired policy and only\n1128: \t// returns changes that need to be applied to the Endpoint's bpf policy map.\n1129: \tcloser, changes := e.desiredPolicy.ConsumeMapChanges()\n1130: \tdefer closer()\n1131: \n1132: \tchangeSize := changes.Size()\n1133: \tif e.shouldLockdownLocked(changeSize) {\n1134: \t\treturn e.startLockdownLocked(changeSize)\n1135: \t}\n1136: \tif e.stopLockdownLocked() {\n1137: \t\treturn ErrComingOutOfLockdown\n1138: \t}\n1139: \n1140: \thasEnvoyRedirect := e.desiredPolicy.L4Policy.HasEnvoyRedirect()\n1141: \tif !changes.Empty() {\n1142: \t\t// updateEnvoy if there were any mapChanges, but only if the endpoint has Envoy\n1143: \t\t// redirects, or is an Ingress endpoint, which needs to enforce also the full L3/4\n1144: \t\t// policy.\n1145: \t\t//\n1146: \t\t// Even if there are no changes, we update the proxyWaitGroup for any in-progress\n1147: \t\t// NetworkPolicy update to be done if the endpoint has envoy redirects, so that the\n1148: \t\t// the expected policy is in place.\n1149: \t\t//\n1150: \t\t// 'updateEnvoy' is already set to 'true' if policy changed. The Endpoint must be locked.\n1254: func (e *Endpoint) shouldLockdownLocked(changeSize int) bool {\n1255: \t// The desiredPolicy will be larger than the BPF maximum after\n1256: \t// the changes.\n1257: \treturn e.desiredPolicy != nil && e.policyMap != nil &&\n1258: \t\te.desiredPolicy.Len()+changeSize > int(e.policyMap.MaxEntries())\n1259: }\n1260: \n1261: // startLockdownLocked initiates an endpoint lockdown, and returns an\n1262: // error if it fails. The bpf policy map is populated with deny all traffic entries,\n1304: // and all other entries are deleted.\n1305: func (e *Endpoint) endpointPolicyLockdown() error {\n1306: \tdenyMap := make(map[policymap.PolicyKey]struct{}, len(allTrafficKeys))\n1307: \tfor _, k := range allTrafficKeys {\n1308: \t\tdenyMap[policymap.NewKey(k.TrafficDirection(), k.Identity, k.Nexthdr, k.DestPort, k.PortPrefixLen())] = struct{}{}\n1309: \t}\n1310: \t// realizedPolicy is not accurrate at this point, we need a dump\n1311: \tcurrentMap, err := e.dumpPolicyMapToMapStateMap()\n1312: \tif err != nil {\n1313: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"could not dump current map state: %w\", err)\n1314: \t}\n1315: \n1316: \tdefer func() {\n1317: \t\te.realizedPolicy = policy.NewEndpointPolicy(e.policyGetter.GetPolicyRepository())\n1318: \t}()\n1319: \n1320: \ti := 0\n1321: \taddedDenyEntries := false\n1322: \tfor k := range currentMap {\n1323: \t\tpmKey := policymap.NewKey(k.TrafficDirection(), k.Identity, k.Nexthdr, k.DestPort, k.PortPrefixLen())\n1324: \t\tif _, ok := denyMap[pmKey]; \tcurrentMap := make(policy.MapStateMap)\n1490: \n1491: \tcb := func(key bpf.MapKey, value bpf.MapValue) {\n1492: \t\tpolicymapKey := key.(*policymap.PolicyKey)\n1493: \t\t// Convert from {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_0183sQ4sbbZcQhh8G6r14W42","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01G5kpBqQGQH3XZHk3GKdQKX","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Cilium eBPF Fault Isolation\n\n## Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle\n\nCilium compiles, loads, and attaches eBPF programs independently on each node with per-node kernel-specific configuration. This isolation is fundamental to Cilium's fault tolerance.\n\n### Compilation (Node-Specific)\n**Component:** `pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go` - The `compile()` function (lines 170-256) and `getBPFCPU()` function (lines 135-157)\n\n- Each node's Cilium agent compiles eBPF programs locally using **clang** targeting BPF bytecode\n- Compilation probes the kernel's capabilities at runtime to determine the appropriate BPF instruction set (v1, v2, or v3) via `getBPFCPU()` which calls `probes.HaveV3ISA()`, `probes.HaveProgramHelper()`, and `probes.HaveV2ISA()` in `pkg/datapath/linux/probes`\n- Configuration headers (`netdev_config.h`, `filter_config.h`) are written per-node with kernel version and feature flags specific to that node\n- **Each endpoint gets a per-node compiled template** via `pkg/datapath/loader/template.go` which creates endpoint-specific maps with names like `cilium_policy_v2_<endpoint_id>` (see `pkg/maps/policymap/policymap.go` line 34: `MapName = \"cilium_policy_v2_\"`)\n\n### Loading and Attachment (Node-Local)\n**Component:** `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go` - Functions `ReloadDatapath()` (lines 700-731), `reloadEndpoint()` (lines 511-583), and `reloadHostEndpoint()` (lines 319-334)\n\n- The `loader.ReloadDatapath()` method calls `l.templateCache.fetchOrCompile()` to compile the program if needed\n- eBPF programs are loaded into the kernel using `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` which loads the ELF binary into that node's kernel\n- **Kernel verifier validation is per-node**: If the verifier rejects a program, it fails only on that node (lines 217-243 in `compile.go` show error handling for compilation failures)\n- Programs are attached to network interfaces via netlink calls to that node's interface (e.g., `attachSKBProgram()` in `loader.go` lines 547-550 for ingress, 553-555 for egress)\n- **Maps are pinned to the node's bpffs**: `ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.TCGlobalsPath()}` (line 347, 395, 447 in `loader.go`) ensures maps persist only on that node's filesystem\n\n### Lifecycle Summary\n- **Compilation Lock**: `pkg/datapath/loader/base.go` line 392 uses `l.compilationLock.Lock()` to serialize compilation and prevent concurrent compilation attempts on a single node\n- **Per-Node State Directory**: `pkg/endpoint/endpoint.go` shows each endpoint has a local `StateDir()` (used at line 704 in `loader.go`)\n- **Node-Local Configuration**: `pkg/datapath/loader/base.go` line 63-74 writes node-specific configuration via `l.writeNodeConfigHeader(cfg)` before any compilation\n\n## Q2: Deployment Architecture\n\nCilium's deployment model isolates each node through **per-node DaemonSet deployment with independent agent lifecycle management**.\n\n### Deployment Model\n**Component:** `Documentation/network/kubernetes/concepts.rst` (lines 18-25), `install/kubernetes/cilium/values.yaml` (lines 219-226)\n\n- Cilium is deployed as a **DaemonSet** resource, which Kubernetes automatically schedules one pod per node\n- Each Cilium agent pod runs independently with its own process, configuration, and state\n- The DaemonSet manifest includes node selectors and tolerations to ensure agents run on specific node types\n\n### Per-Node Agent Initialization\n**Component:** `daemon/cmd/daemon.go` (lines 424-430), `pkg/datapath/loader/base.go` (lines 378-546 - `Reinitialize()` method)\n\n- Each agent initializes the datapath independently via `loader.Reinitialize()` which:\n  - Creates BPF filesystem (bpffs) directory at `bpf.TCGlobalsPath()` (line 413)\n  - Sets up node-specific tunnel devices (line 436)\n  - Applies node-specific sysctl settings (line 449)\n  - Compiles base datapath programs (XDP, socket LB, overlay, wireguard)\n- **Isolation Guarantee**: The call to `l.compilationLock.Lock()` (line 392) ensures only one node's compilation happens at a time, but each node has its own independent initialization sequence\n\n### Failure Isolation Mechanism\n**Component:** `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go` - `ReloadDatapath()` returns error on line 710; if error occurs, only that endpoint on that node fails\n\n- When an endpoint's eBPF program fails to load (e.g., kernel verifier rejects it), the error is scoped to that single endpoint on that single node\n- **Control flow**: `ReloadDatapath()` line 708 calls `fetchOrCompile()` which returns an error if compilation/loading fails\n- The Cilium agent continues running and other endpoints/nodes are unaffected\n- Failed endpoints are logged but don't stop the agent from processing other endpoints\n\n### Control Plane vs. Data Plane Split\n- **Control Plane** (cluster-wide): Policy distribution, identity management via kvstore (etcd/consul)\n- **Data Plane** (node-local): eBPF program compilation, loading, and execution entirely local to each node\n- If one node's agent can't load policies into eBPF, the control plane continues distributing policies to other nodes\n\n## Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement\n\nCilium separates **cluster-wide policy distribution** from **per-node enforcement**, enabling node-local fault tolerance.\n\n### Policy Distribution (Cluster-Wide)\n**Component:** `pkg/policy/distillery.go` - `policyCache` type (lines 15-50) and `pkg/policy/repository.go`\n\n- Network policies are CiliumNetworkPolicy CRDs stored in Kubernetes API server (cluster-wide state)\n- Policies are synchronized to all agents via Kubernetes watchers\n- The policy repository maintains the \"source of truth\" for what rules should exist\n\n### Per-Node Policy Resolution\n**Component:** `pkg/policy/distillery.go` - `updateSelectorPolicy()` method (lines 73-100)\n\n- Each node independently resolves policies for its local endpoints\n- The `policyCache.updateSelectorPolicy()` method:\n  - Calls `cache.repo.resolvePolicyLocked(identity)` (line 94) to resolve policies specific to that node's endpoints\n  - Returns a `selectorPolicy` object that's node-local\n  - Caches the result per-identity (line 24 shows `policies map[identityPkg.NumericIdentity]*cachedSelectorPolicy`)\n\n### Policy to eBPF Translation (Per-Node Endpoint)\n**Component:** `pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` (lines 86-100), `pkg/endpoint/policy.go` (lines 40-53)\n\n- Each endpoint maintains its own policy map at path `bpf.LocalMapPath(policymap.MapName, e.ID)` (line 88 in `bpf.go`)\n- The endpoint ID is local to the node (16-bit number, `uint16` from `endpoint/endpoint.go` line 685-686)\n- **Policy Map Naming**: `cilium_policy_v2_<endpoint_id>` ensures each endpoint has a unique, node-local policy map\n- **Regeneration**: When policies change, only affected endpoints on that node regenerate their programs via `endpoint.Regenerate()` (see `endpoint/regenerator.go` for regeneration logic)\n\n### Compilation Failure Isolation\n**Component:** `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go` line 708-731 - `ReloadDatapath()` method\n\n- If a specific endpoint's eBPF program fails to compile/load:\n  - That endpoint's status is updated to indicate regeneration failure\n  - **Other endpoints continue operating normally** (they use cached compiled templates from `objectCache`)\n  - Policy updates are still applied to other endpoints\n  - The node's agent remains healthy and continues serving other endpoints\n\n### Why Distribution Isn't Blocked\n- **Decoupling**: Policy distribution (kvstore → agent) is separate from enforcement (agent → eBPF)\n- **Asynchronous**: Policy changes trigger endpoint regeneration but don't block distribution to other nodes\n- **Error Handling**: If one endpoint's regeneration fails, the controller logs the error but continues with other endpoints\n- **Endpoint-Specific Compilation**: Each endpoint uses its own cached compiled template (`objectCache` in `cache.go` lines 26-38), so compilation failure in one endpoint doesn't affect others\n\n## Q4: eBPF Map Scoping and State Isolation\n\neBPF maps are **entirely node-local** with filesystem-based pinning ensuring complete isolation across nodes.\n\n### Map Creation and Pinning (Node-Local)\n**Component:** `pkg/maps/policymap/policymap.go` (lines 23-44), `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go` (lines 346-350)\n\n- **Endpoint-specific policy maps** are named `cilium_policy_v2_<endpoint_id>` where `endpoint_id` is the 16-bit Cilium internal endpoint ID (local to the node)\n- Maps are created and loaded via:\n  ```go\n  bpf.LoadAndAssign(&obj, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n      CollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n          Maps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.TCGlobalsPath()},\n      },\n      ...\n  })\n  ```\n  (lines 345-351 in `loader.go`)\n- **PinPath**: Maps are pinned at `bpf.TCGlobalsPath()` which is `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/` per node (kernel's bpffs mounted locally on each node)\n\n### Map Isolation Mechanisms\n**Component:** `pkg/bpf/map_linux.go` - Map struct (lines 65-73), `pkg/datapath/loader/template.go` (lines 159-173)\n\n1. **Filesystem Namespace**: bpffs `/sys/fs/bpf/` is kernel-managed per-node; maps pinned here are only accessible on that node's kernel\n2. **Map Naming with Endpoint ID**:\n   - Template maps use `templateLxcID` (line 164 in `template.go`)\n   - Endpoint maps are renamed using `ELFMapSubstitutions()` which maps `cilium_policy_v2_<template_id>` to `cilium_policy_v2_<actual_endpoint_id>`\n   - Each endpoint's policy map is unique per-node\n\n3. **Per-Device Maps**: Device-specific maps like `cilium_calls_netdev_<ifindex>` (line 221 in `loader.go`) are indexed by the node's local interface index\n\n### Global vs. Endpoint Maps\n**Component:** `pkg/maps/api.go`, `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go` (lines 100-102)\n\n- **Global Maps** (shared across endpoints on a node):\n  - `cilium_lxc` - endpoint metadata indexed by endpoint ID\n  - `cilium_ipcache` - IP-to-identity mapping\n  - `cilium_call_policy` - tail call map for policy enforcement\n  - These are created once per node and reused by all endpoints\n\n- **Per-Endpoint Maps**:\n  - `cilium_policy_v2_<id>` - policy entries specific to that endpoint\n  - Each endpoint has its own isolated map instance\n\n### State Isolation Guarantees\n**Component:** `pkg/endpoint/regenerator.go` (lines 63-87), `pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` (lines 86-100)\n\n1. **Map Failure Isolation**: If endpoint A's policy map fails to update:\n   - The error is caught at `reloadEndpoint()` (line 534 in `loader.go`) which returns the error\n   - Endpoint A's regeneration fails and is logged\n   - Endpoint B's policy map continues operating (it has its own `cilium_policy_v2_<B_id>` map)\n\n2. **Kernel Verifier per Map**: When a program is loaded that uses endpoint-specific maps, kernel verifier checks map compatibility per-program; failure doesn't affect other programs on other maps\n\n3. **No Cross-Node Map Sharing**: Unlike centralized systems, Cilium maps are:\n   - Not shared via network (they're kernel structures in bpffs)\n   - Not replicated to other nodes\n   - Not backed by a distributed storage system\n   - Purely node-local kernel memory\n\n### BPF Links and Pinning\n**Component:** `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go` (lines 760-771, 546)\n\n- TC BPF programs are attached via `bpf_link` structures pinned to `bpffsEndpointLinksDir()` (line 546)\n- Each endpoint has its own directory for links: `bpf.CiliumPath()/<endpoint_id>/`\n- When an endpoint is deleted, its link directory is removed (lines 766-771): `bpf.Remove(bpffsEndpointLinksDir(...))`\n- This ensures no dangling references or cross-endpoint interference\n\n## Evidence\n\n### File Path References\n- `policyCache`, `updateSelectorPolicy()`\n- **Endpoint Policy**: `pkg/endpoint/bpf.go` - `policyMapPath()`, `writeInformationalComments()`\n- **Policy Maps**: `pkg/maps/policymap/policymap.go` - `MapName`, `PolicyKey`, `PolicyMap`\n- **Per-Node Initialization**: `pkg/datapath/loader/base.go` - `Reinitialize()`, `writeNetdevHeader()`, `writeNodeConfigHeader()`\n- **Template Generation**: `pkg/datapath/loader/template.go` - `ELFMapSubstitutions()`, `ELFVariableSubstitutions()`\n\n### Key Class and Function References\n1. **loader struct** (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:74-89`): Wraps per-node compilation and loading state\n2. **ReloadDatapath()** (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:700-731`): Per-node endpoint eBPF loading with per-endpoint error handling\n3. **objectCache** on the same node or any endpoints on other nodes\n\nThis architecture ensures that eBPF datapath failures remain scoped to the affected node, enabling the cluster to continue enforcing policies on other nodes while the failed node either recovers or is capabilities are probed at runtime via `getBPFCPU()` to select appropriate BPF instruction set (v1, v2, or v3)\n- Programs are loaded only into that node's kernel via `ReloadDatapath()` \n- `pkg/endpoint/bpf.go`\n- Compilation failure for one endpoint doesn't block policy updates to other endpoints\n- Policy distribution and enforcement are decoupled\n\n**Q4: eBPF Map Scoping and State node but not across nodes\n- Map failures on endpoint A don't affect endpoint B due to separate map instances\n\nThe analysis shows that Cilium's architecture inherently isolates eBPF datapath
